\"envoy.config.filter.network.http_connection_manager.v2.HttpConnectionManager\";\n\n  enum CodecType {\n    // For every new connection, the connection manager will determine which\n    // codec to use. This mode supports both ALPN for TLS listeners as well as\n    // protocol inference for plaintext listeners. If ALPN data is available, it\n    // is preferred, otherwise protocol inference is used. In almost all cases,\n    // this is the right option to choose for this setting.\n    AUTO = 0;\n\n    // The connection manager will assume that the client is speaking HTTP/1.1.\n    HTTP1 = 1;\n\n    // The connection manager will assume that the client is speaking HTTP/2\n    // (Envoy does not require HTTP/2 to take place over TLS or to use ALPN.\n    // Prior knowledge is allowed).\n    HTTP2 = 2;\n\n    // The connection manager will assume that the client is speaking HTTP/3.\n    // This needs to be consistent with listener and transport socket config.\n    HTTP3 = 3;\n  }\n\n  enum ServerHeaderTransformation {\n    // Overwrite any Server header with the contents of server_name.\n    OVERWRITE = 0;\n\n    // If no Server header is present, append Server server_name\n    // If a Server header is present, pass it through.\n    APPEND_IF_ABSENT = 1;\n\n    // Pass through the value of the server header, and do not append a header\n    // if none is present.\n    PASS_THROUGH = 2;\n  }\n\n  // How to handle the :ref:`config_http_conn_man_headers_x-forwarded-client-cert` (XFCC) HTTP\n  // header.\n  enum ForwardClientCertDetails {\n    // Do not send the XFCC header to the next hop. This is the default value.\n    SANITIZE = 0;\n\n    // When the client connection is mTLS (Mutual TLS), forward the XFCC header\n    // in the request.\n    FORWARD_ONLY = 1;\n\n    // When the client connection is mTLS, append the client certificate\n    // information to the request’s XFCC header and forward it.\n    APPEND_FORWARD = 2;\n\n    // When the client connection is mTLS, reset the XFCC header with the client\n    // certificate information and send it to the next hop.\n    SANITIZE_SET = 3;\n\n    // Always forward the XFCC header in the request, regardless of whether the\n    // client connection is mTLS.\n    ALWAYS_FORWARD_ONLY = 4;\n  }\n\n  // Determines the action for request that contain ``%2F``, ``%2f``, ``%5C`` or ``%5c`` sequences in the URI path.\n  // This operation occurs before URL normalization and the merge slashes transformations if they were enabled.\n  enum PathWithEscapedSlashesAction {\n    // Default behavior specific to implementation (i.e. Envoy) of this configuration option.\n    // Envoy, by default, takes the KEEP_UNCHANGED action.\n    //\n    // .. note::\n    //\n    //   The implementation may change the default behavior at-will.\n    IMPLEMENTATION_SPECIFIC_DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Keep escaped slashes.\n    KEEP_UNCHANGED = 1;\n\n    // Reject client request with the 400 status. gRPC requests will be rejected with the INTERNAL (13) error code.\n    // The ``httpN.downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization`` counter is incremented for each rejected request.\n    REJECT_REQUEST = 2;\n\n    // Unescape ``%2F`` and ``%5C`` sequences and redirect request to the new path if these sequences were present.\n    // Redirect occurs after path normalization and merge slashes transformations if they were configured.\n    //\n    // .. note::\n    //\n    //   gRPC requests will be rejected with the INTERNAL (13) error code. This option minimizes possibility of path\n    //   confusion exploits by forcing request with unescaped slashes to traverse all parties: downstream client,\n    //   intermediate proxies, Envoy and upstream server. The ``httpN.downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path``\n    //   counter is incremented for each redirected request.\n    //\n    UNESCAPE_AND_REDIRECT = 3;\n\n    // Unescape ``%2F`` and ``%5C`` sequences.\n    //\n    // .. note::\n    //\n    //   This option should not be enabled if intermediaries perform path based access control as it may lead to path\n    //   confusion vulnerabilities.\n    //\n    UNESCAPE_AND_FORWARD = 4;\n  }\n\n  // [#next-free-field: 13]\n  message Tracing {\n    option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\n        \"envoy.config.filter.network.http_connection_manager.v2.HttpConnectionManager.Tracing\";\n\n    // This OperationName makes no sense and is unnecessary in the current tracing API.\n    // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n    enum OperationName {\n      // The HTTP listener is used for ingress/incoming requests.\n      INGRESS = 0;\n\n      // The HTTP listener is used for egress/outgoing requests.\n      EGRESS = 1;\n    }\n\n    reserved 1, 2;\n\n    reserved \"operation_name\", \"request_headers_for_tags\";\n\n    // Target percentage of requests managed by this HTTP connection manager that will be force\n    // traced if the :ref:`x-client-trace-id <config_http_conn_man_headers_x-client-trace-id>`\n    // header is set. This field is\n    // a direct analog for the runtime variable 'tracing.random_sampling' in the\n    // :ref:`HTTP Connection Manager <config_http_conn_man_runtime>`.\n    // Default: 100%\n    type.v3.Percent random_sampling = 4;\n\n    // Target percentage of requests managed by this HTTP connection manager that will be traced\n    // after all other sampling checks have been applied (client-directed, force tracing, random\n    // sampling). This field functions as an upper limit on the total configured sampling rate. For\n    // instance, setting client_sampling to 100% but overall_sampling to 1% will result in only 1%\n    // of client requests with the appropriate headers to be force traced. This field is a direct\n    // analog for the runtime variable 'tracing.global_enabled' in the\n    // :ref:`HTTP Connection Manager <config_http_conn_man_runtime>`.\n    // Default: 100%\n    type.v3.Percent overall_sampling = 5;\n\n    // Whether to annotate spans with additional data. And if this flag is set to true,\n    // the tracing provider will assume that Envoy will be independent hop in the trace chain and may\n    // set span type to client or server based on this flag.\n    // This will deprecate the\n    // :ref:`start_child_span <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.router.v3.Router.start_child_span>`\n    // in the router.\n    //\n    // Users should set appropriate value based on their tracing provider and actual scenario:\n    //\n    // * If Envoy is used as sidecar and users want to make the sidecar and its application as only one\n    //   hop in the trace chain, this flag should be set to false. And please also make sure the\n    //   :ref:`start_child_span <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.router.v3.Router.start_child_span>`\n    //   in the router is not set to true.\n    // * If The default value was selected\n  // so as not to interfere with any smaller configured timeouts that may have\n  // existed in configurations prior to the introduction of this feature, while\n  // introducing robustness to TCP connections that terminate without a FIN.\n  //\n  // This idle timeout applies to new streams and is overridable by the\n  // :ref:`route-level idle_timeout\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.route.v3.RouteAction.idle_timeout>`. Even on a stream in\n  // which the override applies, prior to receipt of the initial request\n  // headers, the :ref:`stream_idle_timeout\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stream_idle_timeout>`\n  // applies. Each time an encode/decode event for headers or data is processed\n  // for the stream, the timer will be reset. If the timeout fires, the stream\n  // is terminated with a 408 Request Timeout error code if no upstream response\n  // header has been received, otherwise a stream reset occurs.\n  //\n  // If the :ref:`overload action <config_overload_manager_overload_actions>` \"envoy.overload_actions.reduce_timeouts\"\n  // is configured, this timeout is scaled according to the value for\n  // :ref:`HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.overload.v3.ScaleTimersOverloadActionConfig.TimerType.HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE>`.\n  //\n  // Note that it is possible to idle timeout even if the wire traffic for a stream is non-idle, due\n  // to the granularity of events presented to the connection manager. For example, while receiving\n  // very large request headers, it may be the case that there is traffic regularly arriving on the\n  // wire while the connection manage is only able to observe the end-of-headers event, hence the\n  // stream may still idle timeout.\n  //\n  // A value of 0 will completely disable the connection manager stream idle\n  // timeout, although per-route idle timeout overrides will continue to apply.\n  //\n  // This timeout is also used as the default value for :ref:`stream_flush_timeout\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stream_flush_timeout>`.\n  google.protobuf.Duration stream_idle_timeout = 24\n      [(udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true];\n\n  // The stream flush timeout for connections managed by the connection manager.\n  //\n  // If not specified, the value of stream_idle_timeout is used. This is for backwards compatibility\n  // since this was the original behavior. In essence this timeout is an override for the\n  // stream_idle_timeout that applies specifically to the end of stream flush case.\n  //\n  // This timeout specifies the amount of time that Envoy will wait for the peer to open enough\n  // window to write any remaining stream data once the entirety of stream data (local end stream is\n  // true) has been buffered pending available window. During this grace period, Envoy will\n  // continue to accept new streams. After the grace period, a final GOAWAY\n  // frame is sent and Envoy will start refusing new streams. Draining occurs\n  // either when a connection hits the idle timeout, when :ref:`max_connection_duration\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HttpProtocolOptions.max_connection_duration>`\n  // is reached, or during general server draining. The default grace period is\n  // 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if this option is not specified.\n  google.protobuf.Duration drain_timeout = 12;\n\n  // The delayed close timeout is for downstream connections managed by the HTTP connection manager.\n  // It is defined as a grace period after connection close processing has been locally initiated\n  // during which Envoy will wait for the peer to close (i.e., a TCP FIN/RST is received by Envoy\n  // from the downstream connection) prior to Envoy closing the socket associated with that\n  // connection.\n  //\n  // .. note::\n  //\n  //   This timeout is enforced even when the socket associated with the downstream connection is pending a flush of\n  //   the write buffer. However, any progress made writing data to the socket will restart the timer associated with\n  //   this timeout. This means that the total grace period for a socket in this state will be\n  //   <total_time_waiting_for_write_buffer_flushes>+<delayed_close_timeout>.\n  //\n  // Delaying Envoy's connection close and giving the peer the opportunity to initiate the close\n  // sequence mitigates a race condition that exists when downstream clients do not drain/process\n  // data in a connection's receive buffer after a remote close has been detected via a socket\n  // ``write()``. This race leads to such clients failing to process the response code sent by Envoy,\n  // which could result in erroneous downstream processing.\n  //\n  // If the timeout triggers, Envoy will close the connection's socket.\n  //\n  // The default timeout is 1000 ms if this option is not specified.\n  //\n  // .. note::\n  //    To be useful in avoiding the race condition described above, this timeout must be set\n  //    to *at least* <max round trip time expected between clients and Envoy>+<100ms to account for\n  //    a reasonable \"worst\" case processing time for a full iteration of Envoy's event loop>.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //    A value of ``0`` will completely disable delayed close processing. When disabled, the downstream\n  //    connection's socket will be closed immediately after the write flush is completed or will\n  //    never close if the write flush does not complete.\n  //\n  google.protobuf.Duration delayed_close_timeout = 26;\n\n  // Configuration for :ref:`HTTP access logs <arch_overview_access_logs>`\n  // emitted by the connection manager.\n  repeated The\n   299→  // idle timeout is defined as the period in which there are no active\n   300→  // requests. If not set, there is no idle timeout. When the idle timeout is\n   301→  // reached the connection will be closed. If the connection is an HTTP/2\n   302→  // connection a drain sequence will occur prior to closing the connection.\n   303→  // This field is deprecated. Use :ref:`idle_timeout\n   304→  // <envoy_api_field_config.filter.network.http_connection_manager.v2.HttpConnectionManager.common_http_protocol_options>`\n   305→  // instead.\n   306→  google.protobuf.Duration idle_timeout = 11\n   307→      [deprecated = true, (envoy.annotations.disallowed_by_default) = true];\n   308→\n   309→  // The stream idle timeout for connections managed by the connection manager.\n   310→  // If not specified, this defaults to 5 minutes. The default value was selected\n   311→  // so as not to interfere with any smaller configured timeouts that may have\n   312→  // existed in configurations prior to the introduction of this feature, while\n   313→  // introducing robustness to TCP connections that terminate without a FIN.\n   314→  //\n   315→  // This idle timeout applies to new streams and is overridable by the\n   316→  // :ref:`route-level idle_timeout\n   317→  // <envoy_api_field_route.RouteAction.idle_timeout>`. Even on a stream in\n   318→  // which the override applies, prior to receipt of the initial request\n   319→  // headers, the :ref:`stream_idle_timeout\n   320→  // <envoy_api_field_config.filter.network.http_connection_manager.v2.HttpConnectionManager.stream_idle_timeout>`\n   321→  // applies. Each time an encode/decode event for headers or data is processed\n   322→  // for the stream, the timer will be reset. If the timeout fires, the stream\n   323→  // is terminated with a 408 Request Timeout error code if no upstream response\n   324→  // header has been received, otherwise a stream reset occurs.\n   325→  //\n   326→  // This timeout also specifies the amount of time that Envoy will wait for the peer to open enough\n   327→  // window to write any remaining stream data once the entirety of stream data (local end stream is\n   328→  // true) has been buffered pending available window. In other words, this timeout defends against\n   329→  // a peer that does not release enough window to completely write the stream, even though all\n   330→  // data has been proxied within available flow control windows. If the timeout is hit in this\n   331→  // case, the :ref:`tx_flush_timeout <config_http_conn_man_stats_per_codec>` counter will be\n   332→  // incremented. Note that :ref:`max_stream_duration\n   333→  // <envoy_api_field_core.HttpProtocolOptions.max_stream_duration>` does not apply to this corner\n   334→  // case.\n   335→  //\n   336→  // Note that it is possible to idle timeout even if the wire traffic for a stream is non-idle, due\n   337→  // to the granularity of events presented to the connection manager. For example, while receiving\n   338→  // very large request headers, it may be the case that there is traffic regularly arriving on the\n   339→  // wire while the connection manage is only able to observe the end-of-headers event, hence the\n   340→  // stream may still idle timeout.\n   341→  //\n   342→  // A value of 0 will completely disable the connection manager stream idle\n   343→  // timeout, although per-route idle timeout overrides will continue to apply.\n   344→  google.protobuf.Duration stream_idle_timeout = 24;\n   345→\n   346→  // The amount of time that Envoy will wait for the entire request to be received.\n   347→  // The timer is activated when the request is initiated, and is disarmed when the last byte of the\n   348→  // request is sent upstream (i.e. all decoding filters have processed the request), OR when the\n   349→  // response is initiated. If not specified or set to 0, this timeout is disabled.\n   350→  google.protobuf.Duration request_timeout = 28;\n   351→\n   352→  // The time that Envoy will wait between sending an HTTP/2 “shutdown\n   353→  // notification” (GOAWAY frame with max stream ID) and a final GOAWAY frame.\n   354→  // This is used so that Envoy provides a grace period for new streams that\n   355→  // race with the final GOAWAY frame. During this grace period, Envoy will\n   356→  // continue to accept new streams. After the grace period, a final GOAWAY\n   357→  // frame is sent and Envoy will start refusing new streams. Draining occurs\n   358→  // both when a connection hits the idle timeout or during general server\n   359→  // draining. The default grace period is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if this\n   360→  // option is not specified.\n   361→  google.protobuf.Duration drain_timeout = 12;\n   362→\n   363→  // The delayed close timeout is for downstream connections managed by the HTTP connection manager.\n   364→  // It is defined as a grace period after connection close processing has been locally initiated\n   365→  // during which Envoy will wait for the peer to close (i.e., a TCP FIN/RST is received by Envoy\n   366→  // from the downstream connection) prior to Envoy closing the socket associated with that\n   367→  // connection.\n   368→  // NOTE: This timeout is enforced even when the socket associated with the downstream connection\n   369→  // is pending a flush of the write buffer. However, any progress made writing data to the socket\n   370→  // will restart the timer associated with this timeout. This means that the total grace period for\n   371→  // a socket in this state will be\n   372→  // <total_time_waiting_for_write_buffer_flushes>+<delayed_close_timeout>.\n   373→  //\n   374→  // Delaying Envoy's connection close and giving the peer the opportunity to initiate the close\n   375→  // sequence mitigates a race condition that exists when downstream clients do not drain/process\n   376→  // data in a connection's receive buffer after a remote close has been detected via a socket\n   377→  // write(). This race leads to such clients failing to process the response code sent by Envoy,\n   378→  // which could result in erroneous downstream processing.\n   379→  //\n   380→  // If the timeout triggers, Envoy will close the connection's socket.\n   381→  //\n   382→  // The default timeout is 1000 ms if this option is not specified.\n   383→  //\n   384→  // .. NOTE::\n   385→  //    To be useful in avoiding the race condition described above, this timeout must be set\n   386→  //    to *at least* <max round trip time expected between clients and Envoy>+<100ms to account for\n   387→  //    a reasonable \"worst\" case processing time for a full iteration of Envoy's event loop>.\n   388→  //\n   389→  // .. WARNING::\n   390→  //    A value of 0 will completely disable delayed close processing. When disabled, the downstream\n   391→  //    connection's socket will be closed immediately after the write flush is completed or will\n   392→  //    never close if the write flush does not complete.\n   393→  google.protobuf.Duration delayed_close_timeout = 26;\n   394→\n   395→  // Configuration for :ref:`HTTP access logs <arch_overview_access_logs>`\n   396→  // emitted by the connection manager.\n   397→  repeated accesslog.v2.AccessLog access_log = 13;\n   398→\n   399→  // If set to true, the connection manager will use the real remote address\n   400→  // of the client connection when determining internal versus external origin and manipulating\n   401→  // various headers. If set to false or absent, the connection manager will use the\n   402→  // :ref:`config_http_conn_man_headers_x-forwarded-for` HTTP header. This mode supports both ALPN for TLS listeners as well as\n    // protocol inference for plaintext listeners. If ALPN data is available, it\n    // is preferred, otherwise protocol inference is used. In almost all cases,\n    // this is the right option to choose for this setting.\n    AUTO = 0;\n\n    // The connection manager will assume that the client is speaking HTTP/1.1.\n    HTTP1 = 1;\n\n    // The connection manager will assume that the client is speaking HTTP/2\n    // (Envoy does not require HTTP/2 to take place over TLS or to use ALPN.\n    // Prior knowledge is allowed).\n    HTTP2 = 2;\n\n    // [#not-implemented-hide:] QUIC implementation is not production ready yet. The default value was selected\n  // so as not to interfere with any smaller configured timeouts that may have\n  // existed in configurations prior to the introduction of this feature, while\n  // introducing robustness to TCP connections that terminate without a FIN.\n  //\n  // This idle timeout applies to new streams and is overridable by the\n  // :ref:`route-level idle_timeout\n  // <envoy_api_field_route.RouteAction.idle_timeout>`. Even on a stream in\n  // which the override applies, prior to receipt of the initial request\n  // headers, the :ref:`stream_idle_timeout\n  // <envoy_api_field_config.filter.network.http_connection_manager.v2.HttpConnectionManager.stream_idle_timeout>`\n  // applies. If the timeout fires, the stream\n  // is terminated with a 408 Request Timeout error code if no upstream response\n  // header has been received, otherwise a stream reset occurs.\n  //\n  // This timeout also specifies the amount of time that Envoy will wait for the peer to open enough\n  // window to write any remaining stream data once the entirety of stream data (local end stream is\n  // true) has been buffered pending available window. However, any progress made writing data to the socket\n  // will restart the timer associated with this timeout. This means that the total grace period for\n  // a socket in this state will be\n  // <total_time_waiting_for_write_buffer_flushes>+<delayed_close_timeout>.\n  //\n  // Delaying Envoy's connection close and giving the peer the opportunity to initiate the close\n  // sequence mitigates a race condition that exists when downstream clients do not drain/process\n  // data in a connection's receive buffer after a remote close has been detected via a socket\n  // write(). This race leads to such clients failing to process the response code sent by Envoy,\n  // which could result in erroneous downstream processing.\n  //\n  // If the timeout triggers, Envoy will close the connection's socket.\n  //\n  // The default timeout is 1000 ms if this option is not specified.\n  //\n  // ..
